asked the Prime Minister, Minister of Internal Administrationand Deputy Minister of Defence(a) Is he aware that,

(i) it was stated in the Budget Speech of 2006 thatthe minimum salary increase of the Pensionerswould be Rs. 1,000/- and that an allowance ofRs. 500/- would be added to it; and

(ii) however, what has been given at present topensioners is only an increase of 10% of thesalary drawn so far and an addition of Rs. 500/- thereto?

2006 2712671268

(d) If not, why?

asked the Prime Minister, Minister of InternalAdministration and Deputy Minister of Defence(a) Will he inform this House,

(i) the number of commercial banks operating inSri Lanka as at date;

(ii) whether they are government controlled orprivately owned;

(iii) if so, Government controlled, the names of theGovernment controlled stockeholders?

(b) Will he state

(i) the amount of direct and indirect taxes collectedfrom each bank under different categories forthe last 10 years as a percentage of the totaltaxes collected;

(ii) a comparison of the total taxes against theturnover of each bank as a percentage;

(iii) whether the taxes were increased recently;

(iv) if so, what taxes had been increased and by whatpercentage;

(v) whether it has contributed to increase in thelending rate and to push up the borrowing rate?

(c) If not, why?

( )(The Hon. Nimal Siripala de Silva) , . * .

POTTUVIL MASSACRE INVESTIGATION AND THE GRAVEHUMANITARIAN CRISIS IN THE EASTERN PROVINCE

( [ )(The Hon. Rauff Hakeem)

Bismillahir Rahmanir Raheem

Mr. Speaker, the gruesome massacre of ten innocent Mus-lims in Rathal Kulam, Pottuvil on or about 17th Septem-ber 2006 is being currently investigated by the Criminal In-vestigation Department of the Police. In the meantime, in mycapacity as the Leader of the Sri Lanka Muslim Congress, Ihave addressed a letter to His Excellency the President whilsthe was out of the Island, calling for the commissioning of anindependent, international inquiry into the massacre. I amtabling * this letter and request you, Mr. Speaker, to includeit in the Hansard as a part of my statement.

* . Produced at end of speech.

2006 2716191620

I want to reassure this House that as I have stated in ourletter, this request has been made in good faith with the solepurpose of restoring the confidence in our law and ordermachinery and its accountability to the people. In themeantime allegations and counter allegations relating to theconduct of certain members of our law and order machineryhave been highlighted by the media in the aftermath of thisincident. While it is important to identify the perpetrators ofthis horrendous crime an independent inquiry is also boundto shed light on some issues of social and inter communaldisharmony and the reasons for public outrage relating to theconduct of some officers stationed in the area.

Mr. Speaker, I trust the Government would deal with thisissue dispassionately in order to achieve the objective ofaccountability and transparency in matters relating to lawenforcement and law and order. We also note that the SelectCommittee presently appointed by you to recommend waysand means of prevention of grave crimes should also focusits attention and address matters of concern raised bystatements made to the media by political leaders and seniorsecurity forces officials following this incident.

I would also invite the attention of this House to thehumanitarian crisis that exists in the East in particular. Someleaflet purportedly issued by the LTTE has caused somedegree of panic among the people of Mutur. As a result somefamilies have already left Mutur whilst many others wereforcibly prevented from leaving, by the armed forces. Todaysnewspapers highlight the unfortunate plight of these people.We regret that a Member of Parliament from the JVP whovisited Mutur a few days ago with a government delegation,has levelled a baseless allegation that the SLMC isresponsible for this state of affairs. In the meantime, it isparadoxical to see the LTTE blaming the Government for theleaflet, some ministers in Government blaming the NGOsand the INGOs as being responsible and now the JVP blamingthe SLMC as the perpetrators. And in a strange twist of fate,perhaps for the first time, some Ministers in the Governmentare saying, It cannot be the work of the LTTE since theyhave denied involvement.

It is preposterous to blame the SLMC, while the indecenthurry in which this resettlement programme has taken placeis causing some inevitable repercussions. From the very outset,our position has been that resettlement must take into accountnot only the need for adequate compensation and sufficientlivelihood support, but also the need to create conditions ofnormalcy. An environment of normalcy does not arise bycreating the impression and the ground conditions where theimminent security threat does not exist. It also requires theresettlement of the Tamils in and around Mutur and enablingnormal trade and other social activities between communitiesto resume. Furthermore, substantial lifting of restrictionsimposed on fishing, save and except for those essential forthe security of naval operations, and safe access to theircultivable lands are some of the necessary steps that need tobe taken to improve the imperilled livelihood of these people.

We are also appalled at the manner in which a small numberof families from Mutur, who had sought refuge in Kinniya atAl-Aqsa Vidyalaya and Al-Hira Vidyalaya, have been forciblyevicted by the Police. The refusal to permit voluntary relieforganizations including NGOs as a coercive measure toforcibly resettle anyone who had voluntarily left their homesshould be condemned. We appeal to the Government toinstruct the relevant divisional secretaries to assist thedisplaced families and stop any coercive activity to dislodgethese IDPs against their will.

We would appreciate an official response to this requestfrom the Ministries of Disaster Management and HumanRights and Disaster Relief Services. While theGovernment needs to address these issues in earnestwithout any prevarication and political prejudice, we wouldurge that the Select Committee to Investigate and RecommendSteps to Prevent Man made Disasters be also summoned toenable us to find permanent remedies for these recurringhumanitarian crises.

Thank you, Mr, Speaker.

* : :Letter tabled:

Sri Lanka Muslim Congress

His Excellency Mahinda RajapakseThe Executive PresidentDemocratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka

September 21, 2006

Your Excellency,

Subject - Request for an Independent International Commission of

Inquiry into the massacre of ten innocent Muslims inPottuvil on 17.09.2006

The barbaric killing of ten innocent Muslims in Rattal Kulam, Pottuvilwhich took place in your Excellencys absence in the country, hadearned public outrage and international condemnation.

Following this massacre, the United Nations High Commissioner forHuman Rights, Louise Arbour declared that there was an urgent needfor international community to closely monitor the human rightssituation in Sri Lanka.

Together with IGP, the Commandant of the STF and afew parliamentarians, I visited Pottuvil on September 18, in view ofassessing the situation and pacifying the enraged and distraught civiliansin area.

The following day Hon. Minister A. H. M. Fowzi together with a fewother members of the Cabinet and parliamentarians too went to thearea.

I am sure that the IGP, the Commandant STF and the ministers by nowwould have briefed you about the sentiments of the people in the areaand their attributions as to who was behind the massacre.

On my return from Pottuvil, I had a lengthy discussion with SeniorPresidential adviser Mr. Basil Rajapakse. As the elected representativeof people of the district, I briefed Mr. Rajapakse about the public

16211622

perception of the whole episode. I explained that largely due to a seriesof unhealthy developments in the recent past, the people in the areastrongly suspect that either individuals from or associated with theSpecial Task Force (STF), are responsible for this mass murder.

The Sri Lanka Muslim Congress (SLMC), I pointed out, howeverbelieved that it was too premature to come to such a conclusion andunderscored the need for an independent investigation into the killings,one that would make the aggrieved parties satisfied. It will also helpclear the names of parties which have been falsely accused, if therewere any.

Mr. Basil Rajapakse was sympathetic towards the people, and the reportsabout elements bent on destabilizing the area by exploiting the situation,too were discussed during our meeting.

At the end of the discussion Mr. Rajapakse offered to address theconcerns of the people and help ward off some unfounded fears amongthem.

The SLMC in the meantime is appalled by the haste in which theDefence Spokesman of the Government Hon. Keheliya Rambukwelladismissed our proposal to set up an independent internationalCommission of Inquiry probably misunderstanding our motive behindthe initiative. Our proposal was not made on the basis that there were nocompetence or expertise locally to investigate into the killings, butlargely on the acceptability of the ruling, both locally and internationally,given the accusations made by people in the area. An investigation byan independent international Commission of Inquiry would certainlyadd value and credibility to the proceedings making it transparent andlegitimate.

We at all times acknowledge with great appreciation, the mammothcontributions made by the STF in providing security to a large numberof Muslim villages in the Eastern province. Even the people in Pottuvil,are not apportioning the blame on the STF as an institution, but only onone or two individuals.

Your Excellency would appreciate that this contention of the people asechoed by the SLMC was vindicated by yesterdays indiscriminateshooting at protesting civilians initiated by a few individuals. Surely,the behaviour of these persons is not consistent with the general conductof the STF.

With the precedent set by inviting Australian forensic experts toinvestigate into the massacre of 17 aid workers of Action Contre laFaim, it would be grossly discriminatory if the government moves toignore the local and international request for an internationalcommission of inquiry into the carnage in Pottuvil.

An independent international commission will help the government toregain the lost confidence among the countrys Muslims communityand also the international community, which is awaiting a positiveresponse from the government.

We therefore kindly request Your Excellency to direct the commissioningof an Independent International Commission of Inquiry to investigateinto this gruesome crime. This initiative will certainly help elevategovernment stature internationally and restore good relations with theMuslim community.

Rauff Hakeem M. P.Leader, Sri Lanka Muslim Congress

( )(Mr. Speaker) . .

III

- DESPERATE PLIGHT OF THE PEOPLE AND THE ARDUOUSSITUATION IN THE NORTHEAST

. ( )(The Hon. Mavai S. Senathirajah)

Hon. Speaker, thank you very much for giving me thisopportunity.

Under the provisions of the Standing Orders, I wish tobring the following matters of urgent public importance tothe notice of the House :

1.Currently, there is a severe shortage of food in theNorth - East.

2.There is a severe shortage of other essential itemsincluding medicine, fuel and infant food.

3.The situation has become so acute that people areforced to stand in queues all day to obtain whateverprovisions that are available in very short supply. Thisincludes school -going children numbering over150,000, as a result of which their education has beentotally disrupted.

4.Due to the fuel embargo, none of the local bodies areable to function. As a result, there are severe hygienicproblems that have arisen. This has been compoundedby thousands of civilians living as refugees in camps.This situation has created the danger of epidemicsbreaking out.

5.Transportation has been crippled.

6.Prices of goods have increased over fivefold.

7.There is a severe shortage of cash in banks and as aresult, people are not able to withdraw sufficient moneyto meet the exorbitant prices. Even where people havesufficient money, they are unable to purchase goodsdue to the severe shortage.

8.The Tamil people of the NorthEast and the Tamilpeople of the Jaffna District in particular, are facing ahumanitarian catastrophe due to the economic embargoimposed by the Government.

9.Further, the refusal of the Government to open the A9highway and other roads that link LTTE controlledareas with Governmentcontrolled areas has alsoeffectively crippled businesses in the NorthEast. Thisproblem is worse felt by the business community inthe Jaffna District where the A9 highway is the onlylink the masses could have with the rest of the island.

2006 2716231624

10.Due to this situation, NGOs and INGOs, which havebeen carrying out humanitarian assistance, have alsobeen effectively forced to stop all their work. As aresult, thousands of civilians who have been maderefugees due to the Governments military actions havenot been provided even with temporary shelter andhave been forced to live under trees. This is worst inthe Vakarai and Kathiraveli areas in the BatticaloaDistrict.

11.Amongst all this misery that has been systematicallyunleashed on the Tamil people by the Government,its armed forces are exploiting the situation to themaximum to make profit for themselves. What is worseis that the armed forces of the Sri Lankan Governmentafter systematically and forcibly displacing Tamilcivilians from their homes, are looting these vacatedhomes of all valuables.

12.These actions of the Government are also a directviolation of the Ceasefire Agreement.

If the Government persists with this deliberate policy, therecan be no doubt that the Tamil people will face starvationand death in their hundreds of thousands which wouldtantamount to genocide. Therefore, the Tamil NationalAlliance calls upon the Government to immediately takemeasures to salvage the situation by, one, lifting theeconomic embargo on the North-East and, two, opening theA9 highway and all other roads that link the LTTE -controlled areas with Government - controlled areas.

Hon. Speaker, to express the desperate plight of the Tamilpeople, the TNA Parliamentary Group has decided to carryout a Sathyagraha campaign in this House.

Thank you very much.

The fee should reach him on or before November 30 each year.Late application for subscriptions will not be accepted.
